  public byte[] evaluateResponse(byte[] response) throws SaslException, SaslAuthenticationException {\n    98→        try {\n    99→            switch (state) {\n   100→                case 123→                            callbackHandler.handle(new Callback[]{nameCallback, credentialCallback});\n   124→                            this.authorizationId = username;\n   125→                            this.tokenExpiryTimestamp = null;\n   126→                        }\n   127→                        this.scramCredential = credentialCallback.scramCredential();\n   128→                        if (scramCredential == null)\n   129→                            throw new SaslException(\"Authentication failed: Invalid user credentials\");\n   130→                        String                       throw new SaslAuthenticationException(\"Authentication failed: Client requested an authorization id that is different from username\");\n   133→\n   134→                        if (scramCredential.iterations() < mechanism.minIterations())\n   135→                            throw new SaslException(\"Iterations \" + scramCredential.iterations() +  \" is less than the minimum \" + mechanism.minIterations() + \" for \" + mechanism);\n   136→                        this.serverFirstMessage = new ServerFirstMessage(clientFirstMessage.nonce(),\n   137→                                serverNonce,\n   138→                                scramCredential.salt(),\n   139→                                scramCredential.iterations());\n   140→                        setState(State.RECEIVE_CLIENT_FINAL_MESSAGE);\n   141→                        return serverFirstMessage.toBytes();\n   142→                    } catch (SaslException | AuthenticationException e) {\n   143→                        throw e;\n   144→                    } catch (Throwable e) {\n   145→                        throw new SaslException(\"Authentication failed: Credentials could not be obtained\", e);\n   146→                    }\n   147→\n   148→                case RECEIVE_CLIENT_FINAL_MESSAGE:\n   149→                    try {\n   150→                        ClientFinalMessage It may be safer to throw {@link SaslException} in\n     * most cases so that a standard error message is returned to clients.\n     * </p>\n     */\n    @Override\n    public byte[]         SUPPORTED_EXTENSIONS, scramExtensions.map().keySet());\n                    }\n                    String serverNonce = formatter.secureRandomString();\n                    try {\n Credentials could not be obtained\", e);\n                    }\n\n                case RECEIVE_CLIENT_FINAL_MESSAGE:\n                    try {\n                        ClientFinalMessage clientFinalMessage = new ClientFinalMessage(response);\n                        if (!clientFinalMessage.nonce().endsWith(serverFirstMessage.nonce())) {\n                            throw new              ServerFinalMessage serverFinalMessage = new ServerFinalMessage(null, serverSignature);\n                        clearCredentials();\n                        setState(State.COMPLETE);\n                        return serverFinalMessage.toBytes();\n                    } catch (InvalidKeyException e) {\n                        throw new SaslException(\"Authentication failed: Invalid client }\n        } catch (SaslException | AuthenticationException e) {\n            clearCredentials();\n            setState(State.FAILED);\n            throw e;\n        }\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public String getAuthorizationID() {\n        if (!isComplete())\n            throw new IllegalStateException(\"Authentication exchange has not completed\");\n        return authorizationId;\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public String getMechanismName() {\n        return mechanism.mechanismName();\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public Object getNegotiatedProperty(String propName) {\n        if      throws SaslException {\n\n            if (!ScramMechanism.isScram(mechanism)) {\n                throw new SaslException(String.format(\"Requested mechanism '%s' is not supported. * server side are declared in order, starting with {@link #INITIAL_REQUEST} and\n    99→     * ending in either {@link #COMPLETE} or {@link #FAILED}.\n   100→     * <p>\n   101→     * Re-authentication of a channel on the server side starts with the state\n   102→     * {@link #REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE}. It may then flow to\n   103→     * {@link #REAUTH_BAD_MECHANISM} before a transition to {@link #FAILED} if\n   104→     * re-authentication is attempted with a mechanism different than the original\n    private enum SaslState {\n   109→        INITIAL_REQUEST,               // May be SaslHandshake or ApiVersions for authentication\n   110→        HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST, // May be SaslHandshake or ApiVersions\n   111→        HANDSHAKE_REQUEST,             // After an ApiVersions request, next request must be SaslHandshake\n   112→        AUTHENTICATE,                  //                    // Authentication failed\n   115→        REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE,      // Initial state for re-authentication, processes SASL handshake request\n   116→ 201→        this.saslMechanism = mechanism;\n   202→        Subject subject = subjects.get(mechanism);\n   203→        final AuthenticateCallbackHandler callbackHandler =   236→        } catch (CompletionException e) {\n   237→            throw new SaslException(\"Kafka Server failed to create a SaslServer to interact with a client during session authentication\", e.getCause());\n   238→        }\n   239→    }\n   240→\n   241→    /**\n   242→     * Evaluates client responses via `SaslServer.evaluateResponse` and returns the issued challenge to the client until\n   243→     * authentication succeeds or fails.\n   244→     *\n   245→     * The messages are sent and received as size delimited bytes that consists of a 4 byte network-ordered size N\n   246→     * followed by N bytes representing the opaque payload.\n   247→     */\n   248→    @SuppressWarnings(\"fallthrough\")\n   249→    @Override\n   250→    public void authenticate() throws IOException {\n   251→        if (saslState != SaslState.REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE) {\n   252→            if (netOutBuffer != null && !flushNetOutBufferAndUpdateInterestOps())\n   253→                return;\n   254→\n   255→            if (saslServer != null && saslServer.isComplete()) {\n   256→                setSaslState(SaslState.COMPLETE);\n   257→                return;\n   258→            }\n   259→\n   260→            // allocate on heap (as opposed to any socket server memory pool)\n   261→            if (netInBuffer == null) netInBuffer = new NetworkReceive(saslAuthRequestMaxReceiveSize, connectionId);\n   262→\n   263→            try {\n   264→                netInBuffer.readFrom(transportLayer);\n   265→            } catch (InvalidReceiveException e) {\n   266→                throw new SaslAuthenticationException(\"Failing SASL authentication due to invalid receive size\", e);\n   267→            }\n   268→ case REAUTH_BAD_MECHANISM:\n   284→                    throw new SaslAuthenticationException(reauthInfo.badMechanismErrorMessage);\n   285→                case AUTHENTICATE:\n   286→ state. Current SASL state will be updated when outgoing writes to the client complete.\n   289→                    if (saslServer.isComplete())\n   290→                        setSaslState(SaslState.COMPLETE);\n   291→                    break;\n   292→                default:\n   293→                    break;\n   294→            }\n   295→        } catch (AuthenticationException e) {\n   296→            // Exception will be propagated after response is sent to client\n   297→            setSaslState(SaslState.FAILED, e);\n   298→        } catch (Exception e) {\n   299→            // In the case of IOExceptions and other unexpected exceptions, fail immediately\n   300→            saslState = SaslState.FAILED;\n   301→            LOG.debug(\"Failed during {}: {}\", reauthInfo.authenticationOrReauthenticationText(), e.getMessage());\n   302→            throw e;\n   303→        }\n   304→    }\n   305→\n   306→    @Override\n   307→    public KafkaPrincipal principal() {\n   308→        Optional<SSLSession> sslSession = transportLayer instanceof SslTransportLayer ?\n   309→                Optional.of(((SslTransportLayer) transportLayer).sslSession()) : Optional.empty();\n   310→        SaslAuthenticationContext context = new SaslAuthenticationContext(saslServer, securityProtocol,\n   311→                clientAddress(), listenerName.value(), sslSession);\n   312→        KafkaPrincipal principal = principalBuilder.build(context);\n   313→        if (ScramMechanism.isScram(saslMechanism) && Boolean.parseBoolean((String) saslServer.getNegotiatedProperty(ScramLoginModule.TOKEN_AUTH_CONFIG))) {\n   314→            principal.tokenAuthenticated(true);\n   315→        }\n   316→        return principal;\n   317→    }\n   318→\n   319→    @Override\n   320→    public Optional<KafkaPrincipalSerde> principalSerde() {\n   321→        return principalBuilder instanceof KafkaPrincipalSerde ? @Override\n   343→    public void reauthenticate(ReauthenticationContext reauthenticationContext) throws IOException {\n   344→        NetworkReceive saslHandshakeReceive = 377→\n   378→    private void setSaslState(SaslState saslState, AuthenticationException exception) {\n   379→        if (netOutBuffer != null && !netOutBuffer.completed()) {\n   380→        if (exception != null)\n   388→                throw exception;\n   389→        }\n   390→    }\n   391→\n   392→    private boolean flushNetOutBufferAndUpdateInterestOps() throws IOException {\n   393→        boolean flushedCompletely = flushNetOutBuffer();\n   394→        if (flushedCompletely) {\n   395→            transportLayer.removeInterestOps(SelectionKey.OP_WRITE);\n   396→            if (pendingSaslState != null)\n   397→                setSaslState(pendingSaslState, pendingException);\n   398→        } else\n   399→            transportLayer.addInterestOps(SelectionKey.OP_WRITE);\n   400→        return flushedCompletely;\n   401→    }\n   402→\n   403→    private boolean flushNetOutBuffer() throws IOException {\n   404→ 419→    }\n   420→\n   421→    private void handleSaslToken(byte[] clientToken) throws IOException {\n   422→        if (!enableKafkaSaslAuthenticateHeaders) {\n   423→            byte[] response = saslServer.evaluateResponse(clientToken);\n   424→            if (saslServer.isComplete()) {\n   425→                reauthInfo.calcCompletionTimesAndReturnSessionLifetimeMs();\n   426→ 437→            short version = header.apiVersion();\n   438→            RequestContext requestContext = new RequestContext(header, connectionId, clientAddress(), Optional.of(clientPort()),\n   439→                    KafkaPrincipal.ANONYMOUS, listenerName, securityProtocol, ClientInformation.EMPTY, false);\n   440→            RequestAndSize requestAndSize = requestContext.parseRequest(requestBuffer);\n   441→            if (apiKey != ApiKeys.SASL_AUTHENTICATE) {\n   442→                IllegalSaslStateException e = new requestAndSize.request.getErrorResponse(e));\n   444→                throw e;\n   445→            }\n   446→            if (!apiKey.isVersionSupported(version)) {\n   447→                // We cannot create an error response if the request version of SaslAuthenticate is not supported\n   448→                // This should not normally occur since clients typically check supported versions using ApiVersionsRequest\n   449→                throw new UnsupportedVersionException(\"Version \" + version + \" is not supported for apiKey \" + apiKey);\n   450→            }\n   451→            /*\n   452→             * The client sends multiple SASL_AUTHENTICATE requests, and the client is known\n   453→             * to support the required version if any one of them indicates it supports that\n   454→             * version.\n   455→             */\n   456→            if (!reauthInfo.connectedClientSupportsReauthentication)\n   457→                reauthInfo.connectedClientSupportsReauthentication = version > 0;\n   458→            SaslAuthenticateRequest saslAuthenticateRequest = (SaslAuthenticateRequest) requestAndSize.request;\n   459→\n   460→            try {\n   461→                byte[] responseToken = saslServer.evaluateResponse(\n   462→                        Utils.copyArray(saslAuthenticateRequest.data().authBytes()));\n   463→                if (reauthInfo.reauthenticating() && saslServer.isComplete())\n   464→                    reauthInfo.ensurePrincipalUnchanged(principal());\n   465→                // For versions with rather than authentication exceptions\n   485→                    throw e;\n   486→                } else {\n   487→                    // DO NOT include error message from the `SaslException` in the This avoids\n   514→            // unnecessary exposure to some of the more complex schema types.\n   515→            if (apiKey != ApiKeys.API_VERSIONS && apiKey != ApiKeys.SASL_HANDSHAKE)\n   516→                throw new InvalidRequestException(\"Unexpected Kafka request of type \" + apiKey + \" during SASL handshake.\");\n   517→\n   518→            LOG.debug(\"Handling Kafka request {} during {}\", apiKey, reauthInfo.authenticationOrReauthenticationText());\n   519→\n   520→            RequestContext requestContext = new RequestContext(header, connectionId, clientAddress(), Optional.of(clientPort()),\n   521→                    KafkaPrincipal.ANONYMOUS, listenerName, securityProtocol, ClientInformation.EMPTY, false);\n   522→            RequestAndSize requestAndSize = requestContext.parseRequest(requestBuffer);\n   523→\n   524→            // A valid Kafka request was received, we can now update the sasl state\n   525→            if (saslState == SaslState.INITIAL_REQUEST)\n   526→                setSaslState(SaslState.HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST);\n   527→\n   528→            if (apiKey == ApiKeys.API_VERSIONS)\n   529→                handleApiVersionsRequest(requestContext, (ApiVersionsRequest) requestAndSize.request);\n   530→            else {\n   531→                String clientMechanism = handleHandshakeRequest(requestContext, (SaslHandshakeRequest) requestAndSize.request);\n   532→                if (!reauthInfo.reauthenticating() || reauthInfo.saslMechanismUnchanged(clientMechanism)) {\n   533→                    createSaslServer(clientMechanism);\n   534→                    setSaslState(SaslState.AUTHENTICATE);\n   535→                }\n   536→            }\n   537→        } catch (InvalidRequestException e) {\n   538→            if (saslState == SaslState.INITIAL_REQUEST) {\n   539→                // InvalidRequestException is thrown if the request is not in Kafka format or if the API key is invalid.\n   540→                // If it's the initial request, this could be an ancient client (see method documentation for more details),\n   541→                // a client configured with the wrong security protocol or a non kafka-client altogether (eg http client).\n   542→                throw new InvalidRequestException(\"Invalid request, potential reasons: kafka client configured with the \" +\n   543→                    \"wrong security protocol, it does not support KIP-43 or it is not a kafka client.\", e);\n   544→            }\n   545→            throw e;\n   546→        }\n   547→    }\n   548→\n   549→    private String handleHandshakeRequest(RequestContext context, SaslHandshakeRequest handshakeRequest) throws IOException, UnsupportedSaslMechanismException {\n   550→        String clientMechanism = handshakeRequest.data().mechanism();\n   551→        short version = context.header.apiVersion();\n   552→        if mechanism '{}' provided by client\", clientMechanism);\n   556→            sendKafkaResponse(context, new SaslHandshakeResponse(\n   557→                    new         new SaslHandshakeResponseData().setErrorCode(Errors.UNSUPPORTED_SASL_MECHANISM.code()).setMechanisms(enabledMechanisms)));\n   563→            throw new UnsupportedSaslMechanismException(\"Unsupported SASL mechanism \" + clientMechanism);\n   564→        }\n   565→    }\n   566→\n   567→    // Visible to override for testing\n   568→    protected void      long retvalSessionLifetimeMs = 0L;\n   669→            long authenticationEndMs = time.milliseconds();\n   670→            authenticationEndNanos = time.nanoseconds();\n   671→            Long zeroIfNegative(connectionsMaxReauthMs);\n   679→                else if (!maxReauthSet)\n   680→                    retvalSessionLifetimeMs = zeroIfNegative(credentialExpirationMs - authenticationEndMs);\n   681→                else\n   682→                    retvalSessionLifetimeMs = zeroIfNegative(Math.min(credentialExpirationMs - authenticationEndMs, connectionsMaxReauthMs));\n   683→\n   684→                sessionExpirationTimeNanos = authenticationEndNanos + 1000 * 1000 * retvalSessionLifetimeMs;\n   685→            }\n   686→\n   687→ retvalSessionLifetimeMs);\n   694→            } else {\n   695→                if (sessionExpirationTimeNanos != null)\n   696→                    LOG.debug(\n   697→ 712→            long latencyNanos = authenticationEndNanos - reauthenticationBeginNanos;\n   713→            return latencyNanos == 0L ? 0L : Math.max(1L, Math.round(latencyNanos / 1000.0 / 1000.0));\n   714→        }\n   715→\n   716→        private long zeroIfNegative(long value) {\n   717→            return Math.max(0L, value);\n   718→        }        \n   719→    }\n   720→}\n org.apache.kafka.common.requests.RequestAndSize;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.requests.RequestContext;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.requests.RequestHeader;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.requests.SaslAuthenticateRequest;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.requests.SaslAuthenticateResponse;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.requests.SaslHandshakeRequest;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.requests.SaslHandshakeResponse;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.security.auth.AuthenticateCallbackHandler;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.security.auth.KafkaPrincipal;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.security.auth.KafkaPrincipalBuilder;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.security.auth.KafkaPrincipalSerde;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.security.auth.SaslAuthenticationContext;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.security.auth.SecurityProtocol;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.security.kerberos.KerberosError;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.security.kerberos.KerberosName;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.security.kerberos.KerberosShortNamer;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.security.scram.ScramLoginModule;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.security.scram.internals.ScramMechanism;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.utils.Time;\nimport org.apache.kafka.common.utils.Utils;\n\nimport org.slf4j.Logger;\nimport org.slf4j.LoggerFactory;\n\nimport java.io.Closeable;\nimport java.io.IOException;\nimport java.net.InetAddress;\nimport java.nio.ByteBuffer;\nimport java.nio.channels.SelectionKey;\nimport java.util.ArrayList;\nimport java.util.Date;\nimport java.util.HashSet;\nimport java.util.List;\nimport java.util.Map;\nimport java.util.Objects;\nimport java.util.Optional;\nimport java.util.concurrent.CompletionException;\nimport java.util.function.Function;\n\nimport javax.net.ssl.SSLSession;\nimport javax.security.auth.Subject;\nimport javax.security.sasl.Sasl;\nimport javax.security.sasl.SaslException;\nimport javax.security.sasl.SaslServer;\n\npublic class SaslServerAuthenticator implements Authenticator {\n    private static final Logger LOG = LoggerFactory.getLogger(SaslServerAuthenticator.class);\n\n    /**\n     * The internal state transitions for initial authentication of a channel on the\n     * server side are declared in order, starting with {@link #INITIAL_REQUEST} and\n     * ending in either {@link #COMPLETE} or {@link #FAILED}.\n     * <p>\n     * Re-authentication of a channel on the server side starts with the state\n     * {@link #REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE}. It may then flow to\n     * {@link #REAUTH_BAD_MECHANISM} before a transition to {@link #FAILED} if\n     * re-authentication is attempted with a mechanism different than the original\n     * one; otherwise it joins the authentication flow at the {@link #AUTHENTICATE}\n     * state and likewise ends at either {@link #COMPLETE} or {@link #FAILED}.\n     */\n    private enum SaslState {\n        INITIAL_REQUEST,               // May be SaslHandshake or ApiVersions for authentication\n        HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST, // May be SaslHandshake or ApiVersions\n        HANDSHAKE_REQUEST,             // After an ApiVersions request, next request must be SaslHandshake\n        AUTHENTICATE,                  // Authentication tokens (SaslHandshake v1 and above indicate SaslAuthenticate headers)\n        COMPLETE,                      // Authentication completed successfully\n        FAILED,                        // Authentication failed\n        REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE,      // Initial state for re-authentication, processes SASL handshake request\n        REAUTH_BAD_MECHANISM,          // When re-authentication requested with wrong mechanism, generate exception\n    }\n\n    private final SecurityProtocol securityProtocol;\n    private final ListenerName listenerName;\n    private final String connectionId;\n    private final Map<String, Subject> subjects;\n    private final TransportLayer transportLayer;\n    private final List<String> enabledMechanisms;\n    private final Map<String, ?> configs;\n    private final KafkaPrincipalBuilder principalBuilder;\n    private final Map<String, AuthenticateCallbackHandler> callbackHandlers;\n    private final Map<String, Long> connectionsMaxReauthMsByMechanism;\n    private final Time time;\n    private final ReauthInfo reauthInfo;\n    private final ChannelMetadataRegistry metadataRegistry;\n    private final Function<Short, ApiVersionsResponse> apiVersionSupplier;\n\n    // Current SASL state\n    private SaslState saslState = SaslState.INITIAL_REQUEST;\n    // Next SASL state to be set when outgoing writes associated with the current SASL state complete\n    private SaslState pendingSaslState = null;\n    // Exception that will be thrown by `authenticate()` when SaslState is set to FAILED after outbound writes complete\n    private AuthenticationException pendingException = null;\n    private SaslServer saslServer;\n    private String saslMechanism;\n\n    // buffers used in `authenticate`\n    private Integer saslAuthRequestMaxReceiveSize;\n    private NetworkReceive netInBuffer;\n    private Send netOutBuffer;\n    private Send authenticationFailureSend = null;\n    // flag indicating if sasl tokens are sent as Kafka SaslAuthenticate request/responses\n    private boolean enableKafkaSaslAuthenticateHeaders;\n\n    public SaslServerAuthenticator(Map<String, ?> configs,\n                                   Map<String, AuthenticateCallbackHandler> callbackHandlers,\n                                   String connectionId,\n                                   Map<String, Subject> subjects,\n                                   KerberosShortNamer kerberosNameParser,\n                                   ListenerName listenerName,\n                                   SecurityProtocol securityProtocol,\n                                   TransportLayer transportLayer,\n                                   Map<String, Long> connectionsMaxReauthMsByMechanism,\n                                   ChannelMetadataRegistry metadataRegistry,\n                                   Time time,\n                                   Function<Short, ApiVersionsResponse> apiVersionSupplier) {\n        this.callbackHandlers = callbackHandlers;\n        this.connectionId = connectionId;\n        this.subjects = subjects;\n        this.listenerName = listenerName;\n        this.securityProtocol = securityProtocol;\n        this.enableKafkaSaslAuthenticateHeaders = false;\n        this.transportLayer = transportLayer;\n        this.connectionsMaxReauthMsByMechanism = connectionsMaxReauthMsByMechanism;\n        this.time = time;\n        this.reauthInfo = new ReauthInfo();\n        this.metadataRegistry = metadataRegistry;\n        this.apiVersionSupplier = apiVersionSupplier;\n\n        this.configs = configs;\n        @SuppressWarnings(\"unchecked\")\n        List<String> enabledMechanisms = (List<String>) this.configs.get(BrokerSecurityConfigs.SASL_ENABLED_MECHANISMS_CONFIG);\n        if (enabledMechanisms == null || enabledMechanisms.isEmpty())\n            throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"No SASL mechanisms are enabled\");\n        this.enabledMechanisms = new ArrayList<>(new HashSet<>(enabledMechanisms));\n        for (String mechanism : this.enabledMechanisms) {\n            if (!callbackHandlers.containsKey(mechanism))\n                throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"Callback handler not specified for SASL mechanism \" + mechanism);\n            if (!subjects.containsKey(mechanism))\n                throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"Subject cannot be null for SASL mechanism \" + mechanism);\n            LOG.trace(\"{} for mechanism={}: {}\", BrokerSecurityConfigs.CONNECTIONS_MAX_REAUTH_MS_CONFIG, mechanism,\n                    connectionsMaxReauthMsByMechanism.get(mechanism));\n        }\n\n        // Note that the old principal builder does not support SASL, so we do not need to pass the\n        // authenticator or the transport layer\n        this.principalBuilder = ChannelBuilders.createPrincipalBuilder(configs, kerberosNameParser, null);\n\n        saslAuthRequestMaxReceiveSize = (Integer) configs.get(BrokerSecurityConfigs.SASL_SERVER_MAX_RECEIVE_SIZE_CONFIG);\n        if (saslAuthRequestMaxReceiveSize == null)\n            saslAuthRequestMaxReceiveSize = BrokerSecurityConfigs.DEFAULT_SASL_SERVER_MAX_RECEIVE_SIZE;\n    }\n\n    private void createSaslServer(String mechanism) throws IOException {\n        this.saslMechanism = mechanism;\n        Subject subject = subjects.get(mechanism);\n        final AuthenticateCallbackHandler callbackHandler = callbackHandlers.get(mechanism);\n        if (mechanism.equals(SaslConfigs.GSSAPI_MECHANISM)) {\n            saslServer = createSaslKerberosServer(callbackHandler, configs, subject);\n        } else {\n            try {\n                saslServer = SecurityManagerCompatibility.get().callAs(subject, () ->\n                    Sasl.createSaslServer(saslMechanism, \"kafka\", serverAddress().getHostName(), configs, callbackHandler));\n                if (saslServer == null) {\n                    throw new SaslException(\"Kafka Server failed to create a SaslServer to interact with a client during session authentication with server mechanism \" + saslMechanism);\n                }\n            } catch (CompletionException e) {\n                throw new SaslException(\"Kafka Server failed to create a SaslServer to interact with a client during session authentication with server mechanism \" + saslMechanism, e.getCause());\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    private SaslServer createSaslKerberosServer(final AuthenticateCallbackHandler saslServerCallbackHandler, final Map<String, ?> configs, Subject subject) throws IOException {\n        // server is using a JAAS-authenticated subject: determine service principal name and hostname from kafka server's subject.\n        final String servicePrincipal = SaslClientAuthenticator.firstPrincipal(subject);\n        KerberosName kerberosName;\n        try {\n            kerberosName = KerberosName.parse(servicePrincipal);\n        } catch (IllegalArgumentException e) {\n            throw new KafkaException(\"Principal has name with unexpected format \" + servicePrincipal);\n        }\n        final String servicePrincipalName = kerberosName.serviceName();\n        final String serviceHostname = kerberosName.hostName();\n\n        LOG.debug(\"Creating SaslServer for {} with mechanism {}\", kerberosName, saslMechanism);\n\n        try {\n            return SecurityManagerCompatibility.get().callAs(subject, () ->\n                    Sasl.createSaslServer(saslMechanism, servicePrincipalName, serviceHostname, configs, saslServerCallbackHandler));\n        } catch (CompletionException e) {\n            throw new SaslException(\"Kafka Server failed to create a SaslServer to interact with a client during session authentication\", e.getCause());\n        }\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Evaluates client responses via `SaslServer.evaluateResponse` and returns the issued challenge to the client until\n     * authentication succeeds or fails.\n     *\n     * The messages are sent and received as size delimited bytes that consists of a 4 byte network-ordered size N\n     * followed by N bytes representing the opaque payload.\n     */\n    @SuppressWarnings(\"fallthrough\")\n    @Override\n    public void authenticate() throws IOException {\n        if (saslState != SaslState.REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE) {\n            if (netOutBuffer != null && !flushNetOutBufferAndUpdateInterestOps())\n                return;\n\n            if (saslServer != null && saslServer.isComplete()) {\n                setSaslState(SaslState.COMPLETE);\n                return;\n            }\n\n            // allocate on heap (as opposed to any socket server memory pool)\n            if (netInBuffer == null) netInBuffer = new NetworkReceive(saslAuthRequestMaxReceiveSize, connectionId);\n\n            try {\n                netInBuffer.readFrom(transportLayer);\n            } catch (InvalidReceiveException e) {\n                throw new SaslAuthenticationException(\"Failing SASL authentication due to invalid receive size\", e);\n            }\n            if (!netInBuffer.complete())\n                return;\n            netInBuffer.payload().rewind();\n        }\n        byte[] clientToken = new byte[netInBuffer.payload().remaining()];\n        netInBuffer.payload().get(clientToken, 0, clientToken.length);\n        netInBuffer = null; // reset the networkReceive as we read all the data.\n        try {\n            switch (saslState) {\n                case REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE:\n                case HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST:\n                case HANDSHAKE_REQUEST:\n                case INITIAL_REQUEST:\n                    handleKafkaRequest(clientToken);\n                    break;\n                case REAUTH_BAD_MECHANISM:\n                    throw new SaslAuthenticationException(reauthInfo.badMechanismErrorMessage);\n                case AUTHENTICATE:\n                    handleSaslToken(clientToken);\n                    // When the authentication exchange is complete and no more tokens are expected from the client,\n                    // update SASL state. Current SASL state will be updated when outgoing writes to the client complete.\n                    if (saslServer.isComplete())\n                        setSaslState(SaslState.COMPLETE);\n                    break;\n                default:\n                    break;\n            }\n        } catch (AuthenticationException e) {\n            // Exception will be propagated after response is sent to client\n            setSaslState(SaslState.FAILED, e);\n        } catch (Exception e) {\n            // In the case of IOExceptions and other unexpected exceptions, fail immediately\n            saslState = SaslState.FAILED;\n            LOG.debug(\"Failed during {}: {}\", reauthInfo.authenticationOrReauthenticationText(), e.getMessage());\n            throw e;\n        }\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public KafkaPrincipal principal() {\n        Optional<SSLSession> sslSession = transportLayer instanceof SslTransportLayer ?\n                Optional.of(((SslTransportLayer) transportLayer).sslSession()) : Optional.empty();\n        SaslAuthenticationContext context = new SaslAuthenticationContext(saslServer, securityProtocol,\n                clientAddress(), listenerName.value(), sslSession);\n        KafkaPrincipal principal = principalBuilder.build(context);\n        if (ScramMechanism.isScram(saslMechanism) && Boolean.parseBoolean((String) saslServer.getNegotiatedProperty(ScramLoginModule.TOKEN_AUTH_CONFIG))) {\n            principal.tokenAuthenticated(true);\n        }\n        return principal;\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public Optional<KafkaPrincipalSerde> principalSerde() {\n        return principalBuilder instanceof KafkaPrincipalSerde ? Optional.of((KafkaPrincipalSerde) principalBuilder) : Optional.empty();\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public boolean complete() {\n        return saslState == SaslState.COMPLETE;\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void handleAuthenticationFailure() throws IOException {\n        sendAuthenticationFailureResponse();\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void close() throws IOException {\n        if (principalBuilder instanceof Closeable)\n            Utils.closeQuietly((Closeable) principalBuilder, \"principal builder\");\n        if (saslServer != null)\n            saslServer.dispose();\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void reauthenticate(ReauthenticationContext reauthenticationContext) throws IOException {\n        NetworkReceive saslHandshakeReceive = reauthenticationContext.networkReceive();\n        if (saslHandshakeReceive == null)\n            throw new IllegalArgumentException(\n                    \"Invalid saslHandshakeReceive in server-side re-authentication context: null\");\n        SaslServerAuthenticator previousSaslServerAuthenticator = (SaslServerAuthenticator) reauthenticationContext.previousAuthenticator();\n        reauthInfo.reauthenticating(previousSaslServerAuthenticator.saslMechanism,\n                previousSaslServerAuthenticator.principal(), reauthenticationContext.reauthenticationBeginNanos());\n        previousSaslServerAuthenticator.close();\n        netInBuffer = saslHandshakeReceive;\n        LOG.debug(\"Beginning re-authentication: {}\", this);\n        netInBuffer.payload().rewind();\n        setSaslState(SaslState.REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE);\n        authenticate();\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public Long serverSessionExpirationTimeNanos() {\n        return reauthInfo.sessionExpirationTimeNanos;\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public Long reauthenticationLatencyMs() {\n        return reauthInfo.reauthenticationLatencyMs();\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public boolean connectedClientSupportsReauthentication() {\n        return reauthInfo.connectedClientSupportsReauthentication;\n    }\n\n    private void setSaslState(SaslState saslState) {\n        setSaslState(saslState, null);\n    }\n\n    private void setSaslState(SaslState saslState, AuthenticationException exception) {\n        if (netOutBuffer != null && !netOutBuffer.completed()) {\n            pendingSaslState = saslState;\n            pendingException = exception;\n        } else {\n            this.saslState = saslState;\n            LOG.debug(\"Set SASL server state to {} during {}\", saslState, reauthInfo.authenticationOrReauthenticationText());\n            this.pendingSaslState = null;\n            this.pendingException = null;\n            if (exception != null)\n                throw exception;\n        }\n    }\n\n    private boolean flushNetOutBufferAndUpdateInterestOps() throws IOException {\n        boolean flushedCompletely = flushNetOutBuffer();\n        if (flushedCompletely) {\n            transportLayer.removeInterestOps(SelectionKey.OP_WRITE);\n            if (pendingSaslState != null)\n                setSaslState(pendingSaslState, pendingException);\n        } else\n            transportLayer.addInterestOps(SelectionKey.OP_WRITE);\n        return flushedCompletely;\n    }\n\n    private boolean flushNetOutBuffer() throws IOException {\n        if (!netOutBuffer.completed())\n            netOutBuffer.writeTo(transportLayer);\n        return netOutBuffer.completed();\n    }\n\n    private InetAddress serverAddress() {\n        return transportLayer.socketChannel().socket().getLocalAddress();\n    }\n\n    private InetAddress clientAddress() {\n        return transportLayer.socketChannel().socket().getInetAddress();\n    }\n\n    private int clientPort() {\n        return transportLayer.socketChannel().socket().getPort();\n    }\n\n    private void handleSaslToken(byte[] clientToken) throws IOException {\n        if (!enableKafkaSaslAuthenticateHeaders) {\n            byte[] response = saslServer.evaluateResponse(clientToken);\n            if (saslServer.isComplete()) {\n                reauthInfo.calcCompletionTimesAndReturnSessionLifetimeMs();\n                if (reauthInfo.reauthenticating())\n                    reauthInfo.ensurePrincipalUnchanged(principal());\n            }\n            if (response != null) {\n                netOutBuffer = ByteBufferSend.sizePrefixed(ByteBuffer.wrap(response));\n                flushNetOutBufferAndUpdateInterestOps();\n            }\n        } else {\n            ByteBuffer requestBuffer = ByteBuffer.wrap(clientToken);\n            RequestHeader header = RequestHeader.parse(requestBuffer);\n            ApiKeys apiKey = header.apiKey();\n            short version = header.apiVersion();\n            RequestContext requestContext = new RequestContext(header, connectionId, clientAddress(), Optional.of(clientPort()),\n                    KafkaPrincipal.ANONYMOUS, listenerName, securityProtocol, ClientInformation.EMPTY, false);\n            RequestAndSize requestAndSize = requestContext.parseRequest(requestBuffer);\n            if (apiKey != ApiKeys.SASL_AUTHENTICATE) {\n                IllegalSaslStateException e = new IllegalSaslStateException(\"Unexpected Kafka request of type \" + apiKey + \" during SASL authentication.\");\n                buildResponseOnAuthenticateFailure(requestContext, requestAndSize.request.getErrorResponse(e));\n                throw e;\n            }\n            if (!apiKey.isVersionSupported(version)) {\n                // We cannot create an error response if the request version of SaslAuthenticate is not supported\n                // This should not normally occur since clients typically check supported versions using ApiVersionsRequest\n                throw new UnsupportedVersionException(\"Version \" + version + \" is not supported for apiKey \" + apiKey);\n            }\n            /*\n             * The client sends multiple SASL_AUTHENTICATE requests, and the client is known\n             * to support the required version if any one of them indicates it supports that\n             * version.\n             */\n            if (!reauthInfo.connectedClientSupportsReauthentication)\n                reauthInfo.connectedClientSupportsReauthentication = version > 0;\n            SaslAuthenticateRequest saslAuthenticateRequest = (SaslAuthenticateRequest) requestAndSize.request;\n\n            try {\n                byte[] responseToken = saslServer.evaluateResponse(\n                        Utils.copyArray(saslAuthenticateRequest.data().authBytes()));\n                if (reauthInfo.reauthenticating() && saslServer.isComplete())\n                    reauthInfo.ensurePrincipalUnchanged(principal());\n                // For versions with SASL_AUTHENTICATE header, send a response to SASL_AUTHENTICATE request even if token is empty.\n                byte[] responseBytes = responseToken == null ? new byte[0] : responseToken;\n                long sessionLifetimeMs = !saslServer.isComplete() ? 0L\n                        : reauthInfo.calcCompletionTimesAndReturnSessionLifetimeMs();\n                sendKafkaResponse(requestContext, new SaslAuthenticateResponse(\n                        new SaslAuthenticateResponseData()\n                        .setErrorCode(Errors.NONE.code())\n                        .setAuthBytes(responseBytes)\n                        .setSessionLifetimeMs(sessionLifetimeMs)));\n            } catch (SaslAuthenticationException e) {\n                buildResponseOnAuthenticateFailure(requestContext,\n                        new SaslAuthenticateResponse(\n                                new SaslAuthenticateResponseData()\n                                .setErrorCode(Errors.SASL_AUTHENTICATION_FAILED.code())\n                                .setErrorMessage(e.getMessage())));\n                throw e;\n            } catch (SaslException e) {\n                KerberosError kerberosError = KerberosError.fromException(e);\n                if (kerberosError != null && kerberosError.retriable()) {\n                    // Handle retriable Kerberos exceptions as I/O exceptions rather than authentication exceptions\n                    throw e;\n                } else {\n                    // DO NOT include error message from the `SaslException` in the client response since it may\n                    // contain sensitive data like the existence of the user.\n                    String errorMessage = \"Authentication failed during \"\n                            + reauthInfo.authenticationOrReauthenticationText()\n                            + \" due to invalid credentials with SASL mechanism \" + saslMechanism;\n                    buildResponseOnAuthenticateFailure(requestContext, new SaslAuthenticateResponse(\n                            new SaslAuthenticateResponseData()\n                            .setErrorCode(Errors.SASL_AUTHENTICATION_FAILED.code())\n                            .setErrorMessage(errorMessage)));\n                    throw new SaslAuthenticationException(errorMessage, e);\n                }\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * @throws InvalidRequestException if the request is not in Kafka format or if the API key is invalid. Clients\n     * that support SASL without support for KIP-43 (e.g. Kafka Clients 0.9.x) are in the former bucket - the first\n     * packet such clients send is a GSSAPI token starting with 0x60.\n     */\n    private void handleKafkaRequest(byte[] requestBytes) throws IOException, AuthenticationException {\n        try {\n            ByteBuffer requestBuffer = ByteBuffer.wrap(requestBytes);\n            RequestHeader header = RequestHeader.parse(requestBuffer);\n            ApiKeys apiKey = header.apiKey();\n\n            // Raise an error prior to parsing if the api cannot be handled at this layer. This avoids\n            // unnecessary exposure to some of the more complex schema types.\n            if (apiKey != ApiKeys.API_VERSIONS && apiKey != ApiKeys.SASL_HANDSHAKE)\n                throw new InvalidRequestException(\"Unexpected Kafka request of type \" + apiKey + \" during SASL handshake.\");\n\n            LOG.debug(\"Handling Kafka request {} during {}\", apiKey, reauthInfo.authenticationOrReauthenticationText());\n\n            RequestContext requestContext = new RequestContext(header, connectionId, clientAddress(), Optional.of(clientPort()),\n                    KafkaPrincipal.ANONYMOUS, listenerName, securityProtocol, ClientInformation.EMPTY, false);\n            RequestAndSize requestAndSize = requestContext.parseRequest(requestBuffer);\n\n            // A valid Kafka request was received, we can now update the sasl state\n            if (saslState == SaslState.INITIAL_REQUEST)\n                setSaslState(SaslState.HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST);\n\n            if (apiKey == ApiKeys.API_VERSIONS)\n                handleApiVersionsRequest(requestContext, (ApiVersionsRequest) requestAndSize.request);\n            else {\n                String clientMechanism = handleHandshakeRequest(requestContext, (SaslHandshakeRequest) requestAndSize.request);\n                if (!reauthInfo.reauthenticating() || reauthInfo.saslMechanismUnchanged(clientMechanism)) {\n                    createSaslServer(clientMechanism);\n                    setSaslState(SaslState.AUTHENTICATE);\n                }\n            }\n        } catch (InvalidRequestException e) {\n            if (saslState == SaslState.INITIAL_REQUEST) {\n                // InvalidRequestException is thrown if the request is not in Kafka format or if the API key is invalid.\n                // If it's the initial request, this could be an ancient client (see method documentation for more details),\n                // a client configured with the wrong security protocol or a non kafka-client altogether (eg http client).\n                throw new InvalidRequestException(\"Invalid request, potential reasons: kafka client configured with the \" +\n                    \"wrong security protocol, it does not support KIP-43 or it is not a kafka client.\", e);\n            }\n            throw e;\n        }\n    }\n\n    private String handleHandshakeRequest(RequestContext context, SaslHandshakeRequest handshakeRequest) throws IOException, UnsupportedSaslMechanismException {\n        String clientMechanism = handshakeRequest.data().mechanism();\n        short version = context.header.apiVersion();\n        if (version >= 1)\n            this.enableKafkaSaslAuthenticateHeaders(true);\n        if (enabledMechanisms.contains(clientMechanism)) {\n            LOG.debug(\"Using SASL mechanism '{}' provided by client\", clientMechanism);\n            sendKafkaResponse(context, new SaslHandshakeResponse(\n                    new SaslHandshakeResponseData().setErrorCode(Errors.NONE.code()).setMechanisms(enabledMechanisms)));\n            return clientMechanism;\n        } else {\n            LOG.debug(\"SASL mechanism '{}' requested by client is not supported\", clientMechanism);\n            buildResponseOnAuthenticateFailure(context, new SaslHandshakeResponse(\n                    new SaslHandshakeResponseData().setErrorCode(Errors.UNSUPPORTED_SASL_MECHANISM.code()).setMechanisms(enabledMechanisms)));\n            throw new UnsupportedSaslMechanismException(\"Unsupported SASL mechanism \" + clientMechanism);\n        }\n    }\n\n    // Visible to override for testing\n    protected void enableKafkaSaslAuthenticateHeaders(boolean flag) {\n        this.enableKafkaSaslAuthenticateHeaders = flag;\n    }\n\n    private void handleApiVersionsRequest(RequestContext context, ApiVersionsRequest apiVersionsRequest) throws IOException {\n        if (saslState != SaslState.HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST)\n            throw new IllegalStateException(\"Unexpected ApiVersions request received during SASL authentication state \" + saslState);\n\n        if (apiVersionsRequest.hasUnsupportedRequestVersion())\n            sendKafkaResponse(context, apiVersionsRequest.getErrorResponse(0, Errors.UNSUPPORTED_VERSION.exception()));\n        else if (!apiVersionsRequest.isValid())\n            sendKafkaResponse(context, apiVersionsRequest.getErrorResponse(0, Errors.INVALID_REQUEST.exception()));\n        else {\n            metadataRegistry.registerClientInformation(new ClientInformation(apiVersionsRequest.data().clientSoftwareName(),\n                apiVersionsRequest.data().clientSoftwareVersion()));\n            sendKafkaResponse(context, apiVersionSupplier.apply(apiVersionsRequest.version()));\n            setSaslState(SaslState.HANDSHAKE_REQUEST);\n        }\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Build a {@link Send} response on {@link #authenticate()} failure. The actual response is sent out when\n     * {@link #sendAuthenticationFailureResponse()} is called.\n     */\n    private void buildResponseOnAuthenticateFailure(RequestContext context, AbstractResponse response) {\n        authenticationFailureSend = context.buildResponseSend(response);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Send any authentication failure response that may have been previously built.\n     */\n    private void sendAuthenticationFailureResponse() throws IOException {\n        if (authenticationFailureSend == null)\n            return;\n        sendKafkaResponse(authenticationFailureSend);\n        authenticationFailureSend = null;\n    }\n\n    private void sendKafkaResponse(RequestContext context, AbstractResponse response) throws IOException {\n        sendKafkaResponse(context.buildResponseSend(response));\n    }\n\n    private void sendKafkaResponse(Send send) throws IOException {\n        netOutBuffer = send;\n        flushNetOutBufferAndUpdateInterestOps();\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Information related to re-authentication\n     */\n    private class ReauthInfo {\n        public String previousSaslMechanism;\n        public KafkaPrincipal previousKafkaPrincipal;\n        public long reauthenticationBeginNanos;\n        public Long sessionExpirationTimeNanos;\n        public boolean connectedClientSupportsReauthentication;\n        public long authenticationEndNanos;\n        public String badMechanismErrorMessage;\n\n        public void reauthenticating(String previousSaslMechanism, KafkaPrincipal previousKafkaPrincipal,\n                long reauthenticationBeginNanos) {\n            this.previousSaslMechanism = Objects.requireNonNull(previousSaslMechanism);\n            this.previousKafkaPrincipal = Objects.requireNonNull(previousKafkaPrincipal);\n            this.reauthenticationBeginNanos = reauthenticationBeginNanos;\n        }\n\n        public boolean reauthenticating() {\n            return previousSaslMechanism != null;\n        }\n\n        public String authenticationOrReauthenticationText() {\n            return reauthenticating() ? \"re-authentication\" : \"authentication\";\n        }\n\n        public void ensurePrincipalUnchanged(KafkaPrincipal reauthenticatedKafkaPrincipal) throws SaslAuthenticationException {\n            if (!previousKafkaPrincipal.equals(reauthenticatedKafkaPrincipal)) {\n                throw new SaslAuthenticationException(String.format(\n                        \"Cannot change principals during re-authentication from %s.%s: %s.%s\",\n                        previousKafkaPrincipal.getPrincipalType(), previousKafkaPrincipal.getName(),\n                        reauthenticatedKafkaPrincipal.getPrincipalType(), reauthenticatedKafkaPrincipal.getName()));\n            }\n        }\n\n        /*\n         * We define the REAUTH_BAD_MECHANISM state because the failed re-authentication\n         * metric does not get updated if we send back an error immediately upon the\n         * start of re-authentication.\n         */\n        public boolean saslMechanismUnchanged(String clientMechanism) {\n            if (previousSaslMechanism.equals(clientMechanism))\n                return true;\n            badMechanismErrorMessage = String.format(\n                    \"SASL mechanism '%s' requested by client is not supported for re-authentication of mechanism '%s'\",\n                    clientMechanism, previousSaslMechanism);\n            LOG.debug(badMechanismErrorMessage);\n            setSaslState(SaslState.REAUTH_BAD_MECHANISM);\n            return false;\n        }\n\n        private long calcCompletionTimesAndReturnSessionLifetimeMs() {\n            long retvalSessionLifetimeMs = 0L;\n            long authenticationEndMs = time.milliseconds();\n            authenticationEndNanos = time.nanoseconds();\n            Long credentialExpirationMs = (Long) saslServer\n                    .getNegotiatedProperty(SaslInternalConfigs.CREDENTIAL_LIFETIME_MS_SASL_NEGOTIATED_PROPERTY_KEY);\n            Long connectionsMaxReauthMs = connectionsMaxReauthMsByMechanism.get(saslMechanism);\n            boolean maxReauthSet = connectionsMaxReauthMs != null && connectionsMaxReauthMs > 0;\n\n            if (credentialExpirationMs != null || maxReauthSet) {\n                if (credentialExpirationMs == null)\n                    retvalSessionLifetimeMs = zeroIfNegative(connectionsMaxReauthMs);\n                else if (!maxReauthSet)\n                    retvalSessionLifetimeMs = zeroIfNegative(credentialExpirationMs - authenticationEndMs);\n                else\n                    retvalSessionLifetimeMs = zeroIfNegative(Math.min(credentialExpirationMs - authenticationEndMs, connectionsMaxReauthMs));\n\n                sessionExpirationTimeNanos = authenticationEndNanos + 1000 * 1000 * retvalSessionLifetimeMs;\n            }\n\n            if (credentialExpirationMs != null) {\n                LOG.debug(\n                        \"Authentication complete; session max lifetime from broker config={} ms, credential expiration={} ({} ms); session expiration = {} ({} ms), sending {} ms to client\",\n                        connectionsMaxReauthMs, new Date(credentialExpirationMs),\n                        credentialExpirationMs - authenticationEndMs,\n                        new Date(authenticationEndMs + retvalSessionLifetimeMs), retvalSessionLifetimeMs,\n                        retvalSessionLifetimeMs);\n            } else {\n                if (sessionExpirationTimeNanos != null)\n                    LOG.debug(\n                            \"Authentication complete; session max lifetime from broker config={} ms, no credential expiration; session expiration = {} ({} ms), sending {} ms to client\",\n                            connectionsMaxReauthMs, new Date(authenticationEndMs + retvalSessionLifetimeMs),\n                            retvalSessionLifetimeMs, retvalSessionLifetimeMs);\n                else\n                    LOG.debug(\n                            \"Authentication complete; session max lifetime from broker config={} ms, no credential expiration; no session expiration, sending 0 ms to client\",\n                            connectionsMaxReauthMs);\n            }\n            return retvalSessionLifetimeMs;\n        }\n\n        public Long reauthenticationLatencyMs() {\n            if (!reauthenticating())\n                return null;\n            // record at least 1 ms if there is some latency\n            long latencyNanos = authenticationEndNanos - reauthenticationBeginNanos;\n            return latencyNanos == 0L ? 0L : Math.max(1L, Math.round(latencyNanos / 1000.0 / 1000.0));\n        }\n\n        private long zeroIfNegative(long value) {\n            return Math.max(0L, value);\n        }        \n {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01DkdK3Kr96ScYVfqDxa8NgS","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Perfect! Now I have a complete understanding of the SCRAM flow and the vulnerability. Let me trace through the RFC 5802 specification:\n\nAccording to RFC 5802:\n1. Client sends first message with client_nonce: `r=client_nonce`\n2. Server responds with combined nonce: `r=client_nonce+server_nonce`\n3. Client's final message should echo back the combined nonce: `r=client_nonce+server_nonce`\n\nThe vulnerability in the code at line 151-152 of ScramSaslServer.java:\n```java\nif (!clientFinalMessage.nonce().endsWith(serverFirstMessage.nonce())) {\n    throw new SaslException(\"Invalid client nonce in the final client message.\");\n}\n```\n\nThis checks that the client's final nonce ends with the server's combined nonce. But according to RFC 5802:\n- The combined nonce is: `client_nonce + server_nonce`\n- So the client's final nonce should equal the combined nonce, NOT just end with it\n\nThe bug:\n- The check should be: `if (!clientFinalMessage.nonce().equals(serverFirstMessage.nonce()))`\n- Instead, it only checks `endsWith()`, which could allow an attacker to send a modified nonce\n\nThis is the classic \"nonce tampering\" vulnerability in SCRAM. An attacker could:\n1. Send a client first message with an attacker-controlled nonce (e.g., \"attacker_nonce\")\n2. Receive the server's response with combined nonce: \"attacker_nonce+server_nonce\"\n3. In the final message, send ANY string that ends with \"server_nonce\" instead of the exact combined nonce\n4. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01VX7RdixJqJPcSFhSFDCvb8","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Now I see! The authMessage() method at line 118 builds:\n```\nclientFirstMessageBare + \",\" + serverFirstMessage + \",\" + clientFinalMessageWithoutProof\n```\n\nThe `clientFinalMessageWithoutProof()` includes the nonce that the client sent. Looking at ScramMessages.java line 225-228:\n```java\npublic String clientFinalMessageWithoutProof() {\n    return String.format(\"c=%s,r=%s\",\n            Base64.getEncoder().encodeToString(channelBinding),\n            nonce);\n}\n```\n\nSo the authMessage includes the client's final nonce.\n\nNow let me trace the crypto:1. The client creates a proof using the combined nonce\n2. The server verifies the proof by computing what it should be using the same nonce\n3. The nonce is part of the authMessage, which is used in the HMAC computation\n\nSo if an attacker sends a DIFFERENT nonce in the final message, the proof verification would FAIL because:1. The attacker wouldn't know the correct proof for the modified nonce (they don't have the user's password)\n2. The verifyClientProof() method would calculate the expected proof with the ORIGINAL nonce\n3. The proofs wouldn't match\n\nLet me verify this by looking at the verifyClientProof method again in ScramSaslServer.java (line 228-238):\n\n```java\nvoid verifyClientProof(ClientFinalMessage clientFinalMessage) throws SaslException {\n    try {\n        byte[] expectedStoredKey = scramCredential.storedKey();\n        byte[] clientSignature = formatter.clientSignature(expectedStoredKey, clientFirstMessage, serverFirstMessage, clientFinalMessage);\n        byte[] computedStoredKey = formatter.storedKey(clientSignature, clientFinalMessage.proof());\n        if (!MessageDigest.isEqual(computedStoredKey, expectedStoredKey))\n            throw new SaslException(\"Invalid client credentials\");\n    } catch (InvalidKeyException e) {\n        throw new SaslException(\"Sasl client verification failed\", e);\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThe verification computes `formatter.clientSignature()` using the `clientFinalMessage` (which includes the nonce the client sent), then verifies it against the stored key. So the actual vulnerability is that the nonce check on line 151 uses endsWith instead of equals, but the proof verification itself uses the nonce from the clientFinalMessage, meaning any modified nonce would cause the proof validation to fail.\n\nAn attacker would need to compute a valid proof with a modified nonce, which is impossible without knowing the password. This suggests the vulnerability isn't directly exploitable as a standalone bypass unless there's a way to forge a proof with the original nonce or completely circumvent the nonce validation. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01YWLMK9p7WWk42SpfGs9FUs","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01SSbWim5Amefwutj3YTjVK9","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/triage.md","content":"# Security Reachability Analysis: Apache Kafka SCRAM Nonce Validation Vulnerability\n\n## 1. Summary\n\nThis analysis examines a nonce validation weakness in Apache Kafka's SCRAM (Salted Challenge Response Authentication Mechanism) implementation. The vulnerability exists in the `evaluateResponse()` method of `ScramSaslServer` class, which uses a weak string comparison (`endsWith()`) instead of exact equality matching for RFC 5802 nonce validation.\n\n**Reachability Assessment: YES - The vulnerable code is reachable from external network traffic.**\n\nHowever, the vulnerability's exploitability is **LIMITED** due to downstream cryptographic verification of client proofs that uses the same nonce value. While the weak validation itself is a protocol compliance issue, a complete authentication bypass appears unlikely without the user's password.\n\n**Risk Level: MEDIUM** - Reachable from network, but downstream protections limit immediate exploitation for authentication bypass. However, potential for protocol violation attacks or information leakage remains.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Affected Code\n\n### Location\n- **File:** `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramSaslServer.java`\n- **Method:** `evaluateResponse(byte[] response)`\n- **Lines:** 148-153 (nonce validation in RECEIVE_CLIENT_FINAL_MESSAGE state)\n\n### Vulnerable Code\n```java\ncase RECEIVE_CLIENT_FINAL_MESSAGE:\n    try {\n        ClientFinalMessage clientFinalMessage = new ClientFinalMessage(response);\n        if (!clientFinalMessage.nonce().endsWith(serverFirstMessage.nonce())) {  // LINE 151: WEAK VALIDATION\n            throw new SaslException(\"Invalid client nonce in the final client message.\");\n        }\n        verifyClientProof(clientFinalMessage);\n        // ... rest of authentication\n```\n\n### The Issue\n\nAccording to RFC 5802 Section 7, the client's final message nonce (`r=` attribute) must be **exactly equal** to the combined nonce:\n\n```\nnonce := c-nonce [s-nonce]\n    ;; client's nonce + server's nonce concatenated\n```\n\nThe RFC specifies that:\n1. Client sends: `r=<client_nonce>`\n2. Server responds with: `r=<client_nonce><server_nonce>` (concatenated)\n3. Client's final must echo: `r=<client_nonce><server_nonce>` (EXACT MATCH)\n\n**The vulnerable code checks:**\n```java\nclientFinalMessage.nonce().endsWith(serverFirstMessage.nonce())\n```\n\nThis allows:\n- Valid: `\"abc123xyz+server_nonce\"` ✓ (ends with correct server nonce)\n- Invalid-but-passes: `\"ATTACKER_CONTROL_xyz+server_nonce\"` ✗ (ends with server nonce but contains attacker data)\n\n**Correct validation should be:**\n```java\nif (!clientFinalMessage.nonce().equals(serverFirstMessage.nonce()))\n```\n\n---\n\n## 3. Attack Path\n\n### 3.1 Complete Call Chain: Network Input to evaluateResponse()\n\n```\nNetwork Socket (Client connects to Kafka Broker)\n    ↓\nSocketServer (Java NIO polling loop)\n    ↓\nSelector.poll()\n    [clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/Selector.java:548]\n    ↓\nKafkaChannel.prepare()\n    [clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/KafkaChannel.java:174]\n    ↓\nAuthenticator.authenticate()\n    [clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/SaslServerAuthenticator.java:250]\n    ↓\nSaslServerAuthenticator.handleSaslToken(byte[] clientToken)\n    [Line 286 or 421]\n    ↓\nSaslServer.evaluateResponse(byte[] response)\n    [JAVA SASL API]\n    ↓\nScramSaslServer.evaluateResponse(byte[] response)  ← VULNERABLE CODE\n    [clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramSaslServer.java:97]\n```\n\n### 3.2 SCRAM Authentication State Machine\n\nThe vulnerable code path is triggered in a specific authentication state:\n\n```\nState: RECEIVE_CLIENT_FIRST_MESSAGE (Line 100-146)\n    - Client sends: n,a=<authzid>,n=<username>,r=<client_nonce>\n    - Server response: ServerFirstMessage with r=<client_nonce><server_nonce>\n    - Transition: → RECEIVE_CLIENT_FINAL_MESSAGE\n\nState: RECEIVE_CLIENT_FINAL_MESSAGE (Line 148-163) ← VULNERABILITY HERE\n    - Client sends: c=<channel_binding>,r=<NONCE>,p=<proof>\n    - Server validates: nonce check (line 151) + proof verification (line 154)\n    - Transition: → COMPLETE or FAILED\n```\n\n### 3.3 Network Protocol Flow\n\nThe vulnerability is triggered through the following wire protocol messages:\n\n**Phase 1: SASL Handshake**\n```\nClient → Server: SASL_HANDSHAKE request (mechanism=\"SCRAM-SHA-256\" or \"SCRAM-SHA-512\")\nServer → Client: SASL_HANDSHAKE response (supported mechanisms)\n```\n\n**Phase 2: SASL Authentication Token Exchange**\n```\nClient → Server: SASL_AUTHENTICATE request containing:\n                  ClientFirstMessage: n,n=username,r=<random_nonce>\n\nServer → Client: SASL_AUTHENTICATE response containing:\n                  ServerFirstMessage: r=<client_nonce><server_nonce>,s=<salt>,i=<iterations>\n\nClient → Server: SASL_AUTHENTICATE request containing:\n                  ClientFinalMessage: c=<binding>,r=<NONCE>,p=<proof>  ← NONCE VALIDATED HERE\n\nServer → Client: SASL_AUTHENTICATE response with error or success\n```\n\nThe vulnerable nonce validation occurs when the server processes the third message in the exchange.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Exploitability Assessment\n\n### 4.1 Reachability: YES - CONFIRMED\n\n**Evidence:**\n1. **Network Entry Point:** The Selector polling loop continuously reads from TCP sockets and routes data through KafkaChannel → Authenticator\n2. **Unauthenticated Access:** No authentication is required to reach this code - the SASL handshake itself is the authentication protocol\n3. **Public Listener:** This code is reachable on any listener configured with SASL (default ports: 9092 for plaintext+SASL, 9093 for TLS+SASL)\n4. **No Rate Limiting:** The nonce validation failure at line 152 throws an exception that transitions to FAILED state, but there's no explicit rate limiting on repeated authentication attempts\n\n**Confirmed Attack Surface:**\n- ✅ Can connect from external network (assuming Kafka listener is exposed)\n- ✅ Can send SASL handshake messages (no prior authentication needed)\n- ✅ Can trigger nonce validation code with crafted ClientFinalMessage\n- ✅ Works over plaintext TCP or TLS connections (vulnerability is in SASL layer, not transport)\n\n### 4.2 Authentication Requirement\n\n**Can an unauthenticated external attacker exploit this?**\n\nPartially - with conditions:\n\n**For Nonce Validation Bypass:**\n- ✅ YES - An attacker can send a ClientFinalMessage with a modified nonce that ends with the server's combined nonce\n- ✅ YES - The nonce validation check (line 151) will pass with this crafted nonce\n- ❌ NO - This alone does not constitute a complete authentication bypass\n\n**For Complete Authentication Bypass:**\n- ❌ NO - The proof verification (line 154) validates the authentication token\n- ❌ NO - Proof verification requires knowledge of the user's password\n- ❌ NO - The proof is computed using HMAC-SHA-256/512 over the authMessage, which includes the exact nonce\n- ❌ NO - Modifying the nonce invalidates all previously computed proofs\n\n### 4.3 Attack Scenario\n\n**Scenario 1: Nonce Tampering Attempt**\n\n```\n1. Attacker connects to Kafka broker on 9093 (SASL/TLS listener)\n2. Sends: SASL_HANDSHAKE for \"SCRAM-SHA-256\"\n3. Sends: ClientFirstMessage with username \"alice\" and nonce \"abc123xyz\"\n4. Receives: ServerFirstMessage with nonce \"abc123xyz+SERVER_NONCE_ABC\"\n5. Attacker crafts ClientFinalMessage with:\n   - nonce: \"MALICIOUS_DATA_abc123xyz+SERVER_NONCE_ABC\"  (ends with server nonce)\n   - proof: <attacker computed proof for this nonce>\n6. Server receives message:\n   - Nonce check (line 151): PASSES (ends with server nonce)\n   - Proof verification (line 154): FAILS (attacker doesn't have password)\n7. Authentication fails, connection state → FAILED\n```\n\n**Result:** Attack fails at proof verification stage.\n\n**Scenario 2: Protocol Violation / Compliance Issue**\n\n```\n1. Attacker crafts ClientFinalMessage with any nonce ending in server's nonce\n2. If proof verification were somehow bypassed (DoS condition, code defect elsewhere):\n   - Server would incorrectly accept the authentication\n   - But this requires a defect BEYOND just the nonce check\n```\n\n### 4.4 Mitigating Factors\n\n1. **Cryptographic Proof Verification:** Line 154 calls `verifyClientProof()` which:\n   - Computes HMAC-SHA-256/512 of authMessage\n   - Compares computed stored key with credential's stored key\n   - Uses `MessageDigest.isEqual()` for constant-time comparison\n   - Will fail if nonce is modified (since nonce is part of authMessage)\n\n2. **RFC 5802 Compliance:** Despite weak nonce validation, the combined effect of:\n   - Weak nonce check + strong proof check = effective authentication verification\n   - An attacker cannot produce a valid proof without the password\n   - An attacker cannot modify the nonce without invalidating the proof\n\n3. **Session State Tracking:** The authentication state machine ensures:\n   - Each client connection has its own state (RECEIVE_CLIENT_FIRST_MESSAGE → RECEIVE_CLIENT_FINAL_MESSAGE → COMPLETE/FAILED)\n   - Nonce values are single-use per connection\n   - No nonce reuse across connections\n\n---\n\n## 5. Severity Assessment\n\n### Vulnerability Rating: MEDIUM\n\n**CVSS v3.1 Score: 5.3 (Medium)**\n- **Attack Vector:** Network (AV:N)\n- **Attack Complexity:** Low (AC:L)\n- **Privileges Required:** None (PR:N)\n- **User Interaction:** None (UI:N)\n- **Scope:** Unchanged (S:U)\n- **Confidentiality:** None (C:N)\n- **Integrity:** Low (I:L)\n- **Availability:** None (A:N)\n\n### Justification\n\n**Severity Factors:**\n\n1. **Reachability:** HIGH\n   - Code is reachable from any unauthenticated network connection\n   - No prior authentication required\n   - Public network exposure on default SASL listeners\n\n2. **Exploitability:** MEDIUM\n   - Nonce validation is weak and can be bypassed\n   - However, proof verification prevents actual authentication bypass\n   - Requires knowledge of target usernames and broker configuration\n\n3. **Impact:** LOW to MEDIUM\n   - **Direct Impact:** No authentication bypass for valid users\n   - **Potential Impact:**\n     - Protocol compliance violation with RFC 5802\n     - May indicate other validation weaknesses in codebase\n     - Could be chained with other vulnerabilities\n     - Potential for information leakage through error messages\n     - Potential for rate-limit evasion through crafted messages\n\n4. **Context:** DEPLOYMENT-DEPENDENT\n   - **Higher Risk:** Kafka deployed with public network access + SASL enabled\n   - **Lower Risk:** Kafka in private networks with firewall controls\n   - **Mitigated:** Deployments using mTLS and certificate pinning\n\n### Real-World Impact\n\n**What This Vulnerability Does NOT Allow:**\n- ❌ Unauthenticated access to Kafka cluster\n- ❌ Authentication bypass for valid users\n- ❌ Credential theft or password recovery\n- ❌ Access to Kafka data without valid credentials\n\n**What This Vulnerability Could Enable:**\n- ⚠️ Potential DoS through repeated crafted authentication attempts\n- ⚠️ Information leakage through SCRAM error messages (if error details are exposed to clients)\n- ⚠️ Protocol compliance violation (RFC 5802 non-compliance)\n- ⚠️ Potential stepping stone for combined attacks with other vulnerabilities\n\n---\n\n## 6. Additional Analysis\n\n### 6.1 Code Inspection: Why Proof Verification Protects\n\nThe proof verification in `ScramSaslServer.verifyClientProof()` (line 228-238):\n\n```java\nvoid verifyClientProof(ClientFinalMessage clientFinalMessage) throws SaslException {\n    try {\n        byte[] expectedStoredKey = scramCredential.storedKey();\n        byte[] clientSignature = formatter.clientSignature(expectedStoredKey,\n                                    clientFirstMessage,\n                                    serverFirstMessage,\n                                    clientFinalMessage);  // ← USES clientFinalMessage.nonce()\n        byte[] computedStoredKey = formatter.storedKey(clientSignature,\n                                                       clientFinalMessage.proof());\n        if (!MessageDigest.isEqual(computedStoredKey, expectedStoredKey))\n            throw new SaslException(\"Invalid client credentials\");\n```\n\nThe `formatter.clientSignature()` method computes:\n```\nauthMessage = clientFirstMessageBare + \",\" +\n              serverFirstMessage + \",\" +\n              clientFinalMessageWithoutProof\n\nclientSignature = HMAC-SHA-256/512(storedKey, authMessage)\n```\n\nThe `authMessage` includes the exact nonce from `clientFinalMessage`, so:\n- If attacker modifies nonce to `\"ATTACKER_DATA\" + server_nonce`\n- The authMessage changes\n- The HMAC changes\n- The verification fails (attacker doesn't have the password to recompute)\n\n### 6.2 Test Coverage\n\nThe codebase includes tests that verify nonce validation behavior:\n- `validateNonceExchange()` - tests correct nonce handling\n- `validateFailedNonceExchange()` - tests that invalid nonce throws exception\n\n**Note:** Tests mock the `verifyClientProof()` method, which is appropriate for unit testing the nonce validation component independently.\n\n### 6.3 RFC 5802 Compliance\n\n**RFC 5802 Section 7 Requirement:**\n```\n\"nonce := c-nonce [s-nonce]\n    The nonce attribute value from the client's first message\n    appended with the nonce attribute value from the server's first response.\"\n```\n\n**Kafka Implementation:**\n- ServerFirstMessage correctly concatenates: `clientNonce + serverNonce`\n- ClientFinalMessage should echo this exact concatenation\n- Weak validation using `endsWith()` deviates from RFC specification\n- Correct implementation would use `equals()`\n\n---\n\n## 7. Recommendations\n\n### For Vulnerability Classification\n- **CVE Severity:** Medium (5.3)\n- **Category:** CWE-347 (Improper Verification of Cryptographic Signature)\n- **Type:** Improper Input Validation, Protocol Violation\n\n### For Remediation\n1. Replace `endsWith()` with `equals()` on line 151\n2. Add integration tests that verify nonce exactly matches (not just suffix match)\n3. Review other SASL mechanism implementations for similar issues\n4. Consider adding comprehensive SCRAM RFC 5802 compliance testing\n\n### For Defense-in-Depth\n1. Deploy Kafka with network firewall rules limiting SASL listener access\n2. Use mutual TLS (mTLS) for broker-to-broker and client-to-broker connections\n3. Implement connection rate limiting at transport layer\n4. Monitor authentication failure patterns for attack detection\n5. Keep Kafka updated with security patches\n\n---\n\n## 8. Conclusion\n\nThe nonce validation vulnerability in Apache Kafka's SCRAM implementation is **reachable from external network traffic** and represents a **protocol compliance issue**. However, the vulnerability's **practical exploitability for authentication bypass is limited** due to downstream cryptographic verification of client proofs.\n\nAn unauthenticated external attacker can:\n- ✅ Send crafted SCRAM messages with malformed nonces\n- ✅ Bypass the weak nonce validation check\n- ❌ **Cannot** complete authentication without the user's password\n- ❌ **Cannot** forge valid cryptographic proofs for modified nonces\n\nThe vulnerability should be addressed primarily for **protocol compliance and defense-in-depth**, not due to immediate authentication bypass risk. The weak nonce validation suggests potential quality issues in the SASL authentication layer that warrant broader security review.\n\n**Recommendation:** Fix the vulnerability via RFC 5802-compliant exact nonce matching. Risk level is MEDIUM due to network reachability and protocol compliance concerns, but actual authentication bypass risk is LOW due to downstream protections.\n\n---\n\n## References\n\n1. The vulnerability exists in the `evaluateResponse()` method of `ScramSaslServer` class, which uses a weak string comparison (`endsWith()`) instead of exact equality matching for RFC 5802 nonce validation.\n\n**Reachability Assessment: YES - The vulnerable code is reachable from external network traffic.**\n\nHowever, the vulnerability's exploitability is **LIMITED** due to downstream cryptographic verification of client proofs that uses the same nonce value.
